## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and current concentration A. Classical rate laws express dA/dt as power-law or rational functions of A, with possible time dependence for complex or driven reactions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of single species)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law kinetics)
- First-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with constant source/sink)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Second-order with linear term: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (mixed-order kinetics)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-modulated first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate coefficient)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 + c1 * A**2 + c2 * A (cubic kinetics, oscillatory systems)
- Power-law with time dependence: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (fractal or anomalous kinetics)
- Rational quadratic: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (complex mechanism with saturation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → classical autonomous rate law from mass-action kinetics; try power-law forms in A
- Negative dA/dt values throughout → consumption/decay reaction; rate constant should be negative or rate law has negative sign
- dA/dt proportional to A*(constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth mechanism with a carrying capacity
- Rate that decreases at high A despite increasing A → saturation or inhibition kinetics requiring rational functions like A/(c+A) or A/(c+A^2)
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-autonomous system suggesting time-varying external forcing, photolysis with varying light, or partially reduced multi-species mechanism
- Log-linear relationship between dA/dt and A → indicates power-law kinetics where the reaction order c1 can be identified from slope
- Rate changes sign at specific A values → reversible reaction with equilibrium point; look for (A - A_eq) type terms
- Fractional reaction orders (non-integer power of A) → complex mechanism or chain reaction that has been reduced to effective single-species kinetics
- Rate depends on A but curves in log-log plot → mixed-order or rational function forms rather than simple power law
